Many types of British birds also live alongside the river, although they are not specific to the river habitat.\n</p><p>The Thames contains both sea water and fresh water, thus providing support for seawater and freshwater fish. However, many populations of fish are at risk and are being killed in tens of thousands because of pollutants leaking into the river from human activities.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Salmon" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Salmon">Salmon</a>, which inhabit both environments, have been reintroduced and a succession of <a href="/wiki/Fish_ladder" title="Fish ladder">fish ladders</a> have been built into <a href="/wiki/Weir" title="Weir">weirs</a> to enable them to travel upstream.\n</p><p>On 5 August 1993, the largest non-tidal salmon in recorded history was caught close to <a href="/wiki/Boulters_Lock" class="mw-redirect" title="Boulters Lock">Boulters Lock</a> in <a href="/wiki/Maidenhead" title="Maidenhead">Maidenhead</a>. The specimen weighed <span class="frac nowrap">14<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>2</sub></span> pounds (6.6&#160;kg) and measured 22 inches (56&#160;cm) in length. The <a href="/wiki/European_eel" title="European eel">eel</a> is particularly associated with the Thames and there were formerly many eel traps. Freshwater fish of the Thames and its tributaries include <a href="/wiki/Brown_trout" title="Brown trout">brown trout</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_chub" class="mw-redirect" title="European chub">chub</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_dace" title="Common dace">dace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_roach" title="Common roach">roach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbel_(fish_species)" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbel (fish species)">barbel</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_perch" title="European perch">perch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_pike" title="Northern pike">pike</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_bleak" title="Common bleak">bleak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flounder" title="Flounder">flounder</a>. Colonies of <a href="/wiki/Short-snouted_seahorse" title="Short-snouted seahorse">short-snouted seahorses</a> have also recently been discovered in the river.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The Thames is also host to some invasive crustaceans, including the <a href="/wiki/Signal_crayfish" title="Signal crayfish">signal crayfish</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_mitten_crab" title="Chinese mitten crab">Chinese mitten crab</a>.\n</p><p>Aquatic mammals are also known to inhabit the Thames. The population of <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">grey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harbour_seal" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbour seal">harbour seals</a> numbers up to 700 in the Thames Estuary. These animals have been sighted as far upriver as Richmond.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Common_bottlenose_dolphin" title="Common bottlenose dolphin">Bottlenose dolphins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harbour_porpoise" title="Harbour porpoise">harbour porpoises</a> are also sighted in the Thames.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 January 2006, a 16\xe2\x80\x9318&#160;ft (4.9\xe2\x80\x935.5&#160;m) northern <a href="/wiki/Bottle-nosed_whale" class="mw-redirect" title="Bottle-nosed whale">bottle-nosed whale</a> was seen in the Thames as far upstream as Chelsea. This was extremely unusual: this whale is generally found in deep sea waters. Crowds gathered along the riverbanks to witness the spectacle but there was soon concern, as the animal came within yards of the banks, almost beaching, and crashed into an empty boat causing slight bleeding. About 12 hours later, the whale is believed to have been seen again near <a href="/wiki/Greenwich" title="Greenwich">Greenwich</a>, possibly heading back to sea. A rescue attempt lasted several hours, but the whale died on a barge. <i>See <a href="/wiki/River_Thames_whale" title="River Thames whale">River Thames whale</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcwhale_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcwhale-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_history">Human history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Human history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tower_of_london_from_swissre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tower_of_london_from_swissre.jpg/220px-Tower_of_london_from_swissre.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tower_of_london_from_swissre.jpg/330px-Tower_of_london_from_swissre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tower_of_london_from_swissre.jpg/440px-Tower_of_london_from_swissre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="787" data-file-height="603" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tower_of_london_from_swissre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Tower_Bridge" title="Tower Bridge">Tower Bridge</a>, built 800 years later</div></div></div>\n<p>The River Thames has played several roles in human history: as an economic resource, a maritime route, a boundary, a fresh water source, a source of food and more recently a leisure facility. In 1929, <a href="/wiki/John_Burns" title="John Burns">John Burns</a>, one-time MP for Battersea, responded to an American\'s unfavourable comparison of the Thames with the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi</a> by coining the expression "The Thames is liquid history".\n</p><p>There is evidence of human habitation living off the river along its length dating back to <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> times.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a> has a decorated bowl (3300\xe2\x80\x932700 BC), found in the river at <a href="/wiki/Hedsor" title="Hedsor">Hedsor</a>, Buckinghamshire, and a considerable amount of material was discovered during the excavations of <a href="/wiki/Dorney_Lake" title="Dorney Lake">Dorney Lake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> A number of <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> sites and artefacts have been discovered along the banks of the river including settlements at <a href="/wiki/Lechlade" title="Lechlade">Lechlade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cookham" title="Cookham">Cookham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunbury-on-Thames" title="Sunbury-on-Thames">Sunbury-on-Thames</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history1_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history1-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>So extensive have the changes to this landscape been that what little evidence there is of man\'s presence before the ice came has inevitably shown signs of transportation here by water and reveals nothing specifically local. Likewise, later evidence of occupation, even since the arrival of the Romans, may lie next to the original banks of the Brent but have been buried under centuries of silt.<sup id="cite_ref-british-history1_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-history1-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Britain">Roman Britain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Roman Britain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Some of the earliest written references to the Thames (<a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la"><a href="#Etymology">Tamesis</a></i>) occur in <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>\'s account of his second expedition to Britain in 54 BC,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> when the Thames presented a major obstacle and he encountered the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Belgae" title="Belgae">Belgic</a> tribes the <a href="/wiki/Catuvellauni" title="Catuvellauni">Catuvellauni</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atrebates" title="Atrebates">Atrebates</a> along the river. The confluence of the Thames and Cherwell was the site of early settlements and the River Cherwell marked the boundary between the <a href="/wiki/Dobunni" title="Dobunni">Dobunni</a> tribe to the west and the <a href="/wiki/Catuvellauni" title="Catuvellauni">Catuvellauni</a> tribe to the east (these were pre-Roman <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celtic</a> tribes). In the late 1980s a large <a href="/wiki/Romano-British" class="mw-redirect" title="Romano-British">Romano-British</a> settlement was excavated on the edge of the village of <a href="/wiki/Ashton_Keynes" title="Ashton Keynes">Ashton Keynes</a> in Wiltshire.\n</p><p>In <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span>&#160;43, under the <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Emperor&#160;Claudius</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">Romans occupied England</a> and, recognising the river\'s strategic and economic importance, built fortifications along the Thames valley including <a href="/wiki/Durnovaria" title="Durnovaria">a major camp</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Oxfordshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorchester, Oxfordshire">Dorchester</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cornhill,_London" title="Cornhill, London">Cornhill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ludgate_Hill" title="Ludgate Hill">Ludgate Hill</a> provided a defensible site near a point on the river both deep enough for the era\'s ships and narrow enough to be bridged; <a href="/wiki/Londinium" title="Londinium">Londinium</a> (London) grew up around the <a href="/wiki/River_Walbrook" class="mw-redirect" title="River Walbrook">Walbrook</a> on the north bank around the year 47. <a href="/wiki/Boudica" title="Boudica">Boudica</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Iceni" title="Iceni">Iceni</a> razed the settlement in <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span>&#160;60 or 61 but it was soon rebuilt and, following the completion of its bridge, it grew to become the provincial capital of the island.\n</p><p>The next Roman bridges upstream were at <a href="/wiki/Staines-upon-Thames" title="Staines-upon-Thames">Staines</a>) on the <a href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Highway_(Roman_Britain)" title="Devil&#39;s Highway (Roman Britain)">Devil\'s Highway</a> between Londinium and <a href="/wiki/Calleva_Atrebatum" title="Calleva Atrebatum">Calleva</a> (<a href="/wiki/Silchester" title="Silchester">Silchester</a>). Boats could be swept up to it on the rising tide with no need for wind or muscle power.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A Romano-British settlement grew up north of the confluence, partly because the site was naturally protected from attack on the east side by the <a href="/wiki/River_Cherwell" title="River Cherwell">River Cherwell</a> and on the west by the River Thames. This settlement dominated the pottery trade in what is now central southern England, and pottery was distributed by boats on the Thames and its tributaries.\n</p><p>Competition for the use of the river created the centuries-old conflict between those who wanted to dam the river to build millraces and fish traps and those who wanted to travel and carry goods on it. Economic prosperity and the foundation of wealthy monasteries by the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a> attracted unwelcome visitors and by around AD 870 the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> were sweeping up the Thames on the tide and creating havoc as in their destruction of <a href="/wiki/Chertsey_Abbey" title="Chertsey Abbey">Chertsey Abbey</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Bridge_(1616)_by_Claes_Van_Visscher.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/London_Bridge_%281616%29_by_Claes_Van_Visscher.jpg/220px-London_Bridge_%281616%29_by_Claes_Van_Visscher.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/London_Bridge_%281616%29_by_Claes_Van_Visscher.jpg/330px-London_Bridge_%281616%29_by_Claes_Van_Visscher.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/London_Bridge_%281616%29_by_Claes_Van_Visscher.jpg/440px-London_Bridge_%281616%29_by_Claes_Van_Visscher.jpg 2x" data-file-width="665" data-file-height="442" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_Bridge_(1616)_by_Claes_Van_Visscher.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1616 engraving by <a href="/wiki/Claes_Van_Visscher" class="mw-redirect" title="Claes Van Visscher">Claes Van Visscher</a> showing the <a href="/wiki/Old_London_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Old London Bridge">Old London Bridge</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Southwark_Cathedral" title="Southwark Cathedral">Southwark Cathedral</a> in the foreground</div></div></div>\n<p>Once <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="William I of England">King William</a> had won total control of the strategically important Thames Valley, he went on to invade the rest of England. He had many castles built, including those at <a href="/wiki/Wallingford_Castle" title="Wallingford Castle">Wallingford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_Kent" title="Rochester, Kent">Rochester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Berkshire" title="Windsor, Berkshire">Windsor</a> and most importantly the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a>. Many details of Thames activity are recorded in the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a>. The following centuries saw the conflict between king and barons coming to a head in AD 1215 when <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">King John</a> was forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carta" title="Magna Carta">Magna Carta</a> on an island in the Thames at <a href="/wiki/Runnymede" title="Runnymede">Runnymede</a>. Among a host of other things, this granted the barons the right of Navigation under Clause 23.\n</p><p>Another major consequence of John\'s reign was the completion of the multi-piered <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge" title="London Bridge">London Bridge</a>, which acted as a barricade and barrage on the river, affecting the tidal flow upstream and increasing the likelihood of the river freezing over. In <a href="/wiki/Tudor_period" title="Tudor period">Tudor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stuart_period" title="Stuart period">Stuart</a> times, various kings and queens built magnificent riverside palaces at <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Court_Palace" title="Hampton Court Palace">Hampton Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kew" title="Kew">Kew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richmond_on_Thames" class="mw-redirect" title="Richmond on Thames">Richmond on Thames</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitehall" title="Whitehall">Whitehall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenwich" title="Greenwich">Greenwich</a>.\n</p><p>As early as the 1300s, the Thames was used to dispose of waste matter produced in the city of London, thus turning the river into an open sewer. In 1357, <a href="/wiki/Edward_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward III">Edward III</a> described the state of the river in a proclamation: "... dung and other filth had accumulated in divers places upon the banks of the river with ... fumes and other abominable stenches arising therefrom."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2007_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2007-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The growth of the population of London greatly increased the amount of waste that entered the river, including human excrement, animal waste from slaughter houses, and waste from manufacturing processes. According to historian Peter Ackroyd, "a public lavatory on London Bridge showered its contents directly onto the river below, and latrines were built over all the tributaries that issued into the Thames."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2007_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2007-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Frozen_Thames_1677.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Frozen_Thames_1677.jpg/220px-The_Frozen_Thames_1677.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Frozen_Thames_1677.jpg/330px-The_Frozen_Thames_1677.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Frozen_Thames_1677.jpg/440px-The_Frozen_Thames_1677.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="371" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Frozen_Thames_1677.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Frozen Thames</i>, 1677</div></div></div>\n<p>During a series of cold winters the Thames froze over above London Bridge: in the first <a href="/wiki/Thames_frost_fairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Thames frost fairs">Frost Fair</a> in 1607, a tent city was set up on the river, along with a number of amusements, including ice bowling.\n</p><p>In good conditions, barges travelled daily from Oxford to London carrying timber, wool, foodstuffs and livestock. The stone from the <a href="/wiki/Cotswolds" title="Cotswolds">Cotswolds</a> used to rebuild <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul&#39;s Cathedral">St Paul\'s Cathedral</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_London" title="Great Fire of London">Great Fire</a> in 1666 was brought all the way down from <a href="/wiki/Radcot" class="mw-redirect" title="Radcot">Radcot</a>. The Thames provided the major route between the City of London and Westminster in the 16th and 17th centuries; the clannish guild of watermen ferried Londoners from landing to landing and tolerated no outside interference. In 1715, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Doggett" title="Thomas Doggett">Thomas Doggett</a> was so grateful to a local waterman for his efforts in ferrying him home, pulling against the tide, that he set up a rowing race for professional watermen known as "<a href="/wiki/Doggett%27s_Coat_and_Badge" title="Doggett&#39;s Coat and Badge">Doggett\'s Coat and Badge</a>".\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FaradayFatherThames.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/FaradayFatherThames.jpg/220px-FaradayFatherThames.jpg" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/FaradayFatherThames.jpg/330px-FaradayFatherThames.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/FaradayFatherThames.jpg 2x" data-file-width="396" data-file-height="584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FaradayFatherThames.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Michael_Faraday" title="Michael Faraday">Michael Faraday</a> giving his card to Father Thames</i>, caricature commenting on a letter of Faraday\'s <a href="/wiki/Great_Stink" title="Great Stink">on the state of the river</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> in July 1855</div></div></div>\n<p>By the 18th century, the Thames was one of the world\'s busiest waterways, as London became the centre of the vast, mercantile <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, and progressively over the next century the docks expanded in the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Dogs" title="Isle of Dogs">Isle of Dogs</a> and beyond. Efforts were made to resolve the navigation conflicts upstream by building locks along the Thames. After temperatures began to rise again, starting in 1814, the river stopped freezing over.<sup id="cite_ref-freeze2_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freeze2-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The building of a new <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge" title="London Bridge">London Bridge</a> in 1825, with fewer <a href="/wiki/Pier_(architecture)" title="Pier (architecture)">piers</a> (pillars) than the old, allowed the river to flow more freely and prevented it from freezing over in cold winters.<sup id="cite_ref-freeze1_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freeze1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Throughout early modern history the population of London and its industries discarded their rubbish in the river.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> This included the waste from slaughterhouses, fish markets, and tanneries. The buildup in household cesspools could sometimes overflow, especially when it rained, and was washed into London\'s streets and sewers which eventually led to the Thames.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In the late 18th and 19th centuries people known as <a href="/wiki/Mudlark" title="Mudlark">Mudlarks</a> scavenged in the river mud for a meagre living.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Victorian_era">Victorian era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Victorian era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Monster_Soup_commonly_called_Thames_Water._Wellcome_V0011218.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Monster_Soup_commonly_called_Thames_Water._Wellcome_V0011218.jpg/220px-Monster_Soup_commonly_called_Thames_Water._Wellcome_V0011218.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Monster_Soup_commonly_called_Thames_Water._Wellcome_V0011218.jpg/330px-Monster_Soup_commonly_called_Thames_Water._Wellcome_V0011218.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Monster_Soup_commonly_called_Thames_Water._Wellcome_V0011218.jpg/440px-Monster_Soup_commonly_called_Thames_Water._Wellcome_V0011218.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3485" data-file-height="2370" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Monster_Soup_commonly_called_Thames_Water._Wellcome_V0011218.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satirical cartoon by <a href="/wiki/William_Heath_(artist)" title="William Heath (artist)">William Heath</a>, showing a woman observing monsters in a drop of London water (at the time of the <i>Commission on the London Water Supply</i> report, 1828)</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 19th century the quality of water in Thames deteriorated further. The dumping of raw <a href="/wiki/Sewage" title="Sewage">sewage</a> into the Thames was formerly only common in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_London" title="City of London">City of London</a>, making its tideway a harbour for many harmful bacteria. Gas manufactories were built alongside the river, and their by-products leaked into the water, including spent lime, ammonia, cyanide, and carbolic acid. The river had an unnaturally warm temperature caused by chemical reactions in the water, which also removed the water\'s oxygen.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Four serious cholera outbreaks killed tens of thousands of people between 1832 and 1865. Historians have attributed <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Prince_Consort" title="Albert, Prince Consort">Prince Albert\'s</a> death in 1861 to typhoid that had spread in the river\'s dirty waters beside Windsor Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Wells with <a href="/wiki/Water_table" title="Water table">water tables</a> that mixed with tributaries (or the non-tidal Thames) faced such pollution with the widespread installation of the <a href="/wiki/Flush_toilet" title="Flush toilet">flush toilet</a> in the 1850s.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>  In the \'<a href="/wiki/Great_Stink" title="Great Stink">Great Stink\' of 1858</a>, pollution in the river reached such an extreme that sittings of the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> at Westminster had to be abandoned. Chlorine-soaked drapes were hung in the windows of Parliament in an attempt to stave off the smell of the river, but to no avail.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A concerted effort to contain the city\'s sewage by constructing massive <a href="/wiki/Combined_sewer" title="Combined sewer">sewer systems</a> on the north and south river embankments followed, under the supervision of engineer <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bazalgette" title="Joseph Bazalgette">Joseph Bazalgette</a>. Meanwhile, similar huge undertakings took place to ensure the water supply, with the building of reservoirs and pumping stations on the river to the west of London, slowly helping the quality of water to improve.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> was one of imaginative engineering. The coming of the railways added railway bridges to the earlier road bridges and also reduced commercial activity on the river. However, sporting and leisure use increased with the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Regatta" title="Regatta">regattas</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Henley_Royal_Regatta" title="Henley Royal Regatta">Henley</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Boat_Race" title="The Boat Race">the Boat Race</a>. On 3 September 1878, one of the worst river disasters in England took place, when the crowded pleasure boat <a href="/wiki/SS_Princess_Alice_(1865)" title="SS Princess Alice (1865)"><i>Princess Alice</i></a> collided with the <i>Bywell Castle</i>, killing over 640 people.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_from_above_MLD_051002_003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/London_from_above_MLD_051002_003.jpg/220px-London_from_above_MLD_051002_003.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/London_from_above_MLD_051002_003.jpg/330px-London_from_above_MLD_051002_003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/London_from_above_MLD_051002_003.jpg/440px-London_from_above_MLD_051002_003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1352" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_from_above_MLD_051002_003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Thames as it flows through east London, with the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Dogs" title="Isle of Dogs">Isle of Dogs</a> in the centre</div></div></div>\n<p>The growth of <a href="/wiki/Road_transport" title="Road transport">road transport</a>, and the decline of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Empire</a> in the years following 1914, reduced the economic prominence of the river. During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, the protection of certain Thames-side facilities, particularly docks and water treatment plants, was crucial to the munitions and water supply of the country. The river\'s defences included the <a href="/wiki/Maunsell_fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Maunsell fort">Maunsell forts</a> in the estuary, and the use of <a href="/wiki/Barrage_balloons" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrage balloons">barrage balloons</a> to counter <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">German bombers</a> using the reflectivity and shapes of the river to navigate during <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>.\n</p><p>In the post-war era, although the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_London#The_Port_today" title="Port of London">Port of London</a> remains one of the UK\'s three main ports, most trade has moved downstream from central London. In the late 1950s, the discharge of methane gas in the depths of the river caused the water to bubble, and the toxins wore away at boats\' propellers.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The decline of heavy industry and tanneries, reduced use of oil-pollutants and improved sewage treatment have led to much better water quality as compared with the late 19th and early- to mid-20th centuries and aquatic life has returned to its formerly \'dead\' stretches.\n</p><p>Alongside the entire river runs the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Path" title="Thames Path">Thames Path</a>, a National Route for walkers and cyclists.\n</p><p>In the early 1980s a pioneering flood control device, the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Barrier" title="Thames Barrier">Thames Barrier</a>, was opened. It is closed to tides several times a year to prevent water damage to London\'s low-lying areas upstream (the <a href="/wiki/1928_Thames_flood" title="1928 Thames flood">1928 Thames flood</a> demonstrated the severity of this type of event).\n</p><p>In the late 1990s, the 7-mile (11&#160;km) long <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_River" title="Jubilee River">Jubilee River</a> was built as a wide "naturalistic" flood relief channel from <a href="/wiki/Taplow" title="Taplow">Taplow</a> to <a href="/wiki/Eton,_Berkshire" title="Eton, Berkshire">Eton</a> to help reduce the flood risk in <a href="/wiki/Maidenhead" title="Maidenhead">Maidenhead</a> <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Berkshire" title="Windsor, Berkshire">Windsor</a> and Eton.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, the Thames won the largest environmental award in the world \xe2\x80\x93 the $350,000 International Riverprize.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_active_river">The active river</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The active river">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Houseboats_-_Richmond,_London,_UK.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Houseboats_-_Richmond%2C_London%2C_UK.jpg/220px-Houseboats_-_Richmond%2C_London%2C_UK.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Houseboats_-_Richmond%2C_London%2C_UK.jpg/330px-Houseboats_-_Richmond%2C_London%2C_UK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Houseboats_-_Richmond%2C_London%2C_UK.jpg/440px-Houseboats_-_Richmond%2C_London%2C_UK.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1952" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Houseboats_-_Richmond,_London,_UK.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Houseboat" title="Houseboat">Houseboats</a> on the River Thames, in the <a href="/wiki/St_Margarets,_London" title="St Margarets, London">St Margaret\'s, Twickenham</a> district</div></div></div>\n<p>One of the major resources provided by the Thames is the water distributed as drinking water by <a href="/wiki/Thames_Water" title="Thames Water">Thames Water</a>, whose area of responsibility covers the length of the River Thames. The <a href="/wiki/Thames_Water_Ring_Main" title="Thames Water Ring Main">Thames Water Ring Main</a> is the main distribution mechanism for water in London, with one major loop linking the <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_London" title="Hampton, London">Hampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walton-on-Thames" title="Walton-on-Thames">Walton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashford,_Surrey" title="Ashford, Surrey">Ashford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kempton_Park,_Surrey" title="Kempton Park, Surrey">Kempton Park</a> Water Treatment Works with central London.\n</p><p>In the past, commercial activities on the Thames included fishing (particularly eel trapping), <a href="/wiki/Coppicing" title="Coppicing">coppicing</a> <a href="/wiki/Willow" title="Willow">willows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willow" title="Willow">osiers</a> which provided wood, and the operation of <a href="/wiki/Watermill" title="Watermill">watermills</a> for flour and paper production and metal beating. These activities have disappeared. A <a href="/wiki/Screw_turbine" title="Screw turbine">screw turbine</a> hydro-electric plant at <a href="/wiki/Romney_Lock" title="Romney Lock">Romney Lock</a> to power <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a> using two <a href="/wiki/Archimedes%27_screw" title="Archimedes&#39; screw">Archimedes\' screws</a> was opened in 2013 by the Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Thames is popular for a wide variety of riverside housing, including high-rise flats in central London and chalets on the banks and islands upstream. Some people live in houseboats, typically around <a href="/wiki/Brentford" title="Brentford">Brentford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tagg%27s_Island" title="Tagg&#39;s Island">Tagg\'s Island</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_and_tourism">Transport and tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport and tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_tidal_river">The tidal river</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: The tidal river">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/London_River_Services" title="London River Services">London River Services</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterloo_Pier_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Waterloo_Pier_1.jpg/220px-Waterloo_Pier_1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Waterloo_Pier_1.jpg/330px-Waterloo_Pier_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Waterloo_Pier_1.jpg/440px-Waterloo_Pier_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1741" data-file-height="1158" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterloo_Pier_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Passenger service on the River Thames</div></div></div>\n<p>In London there are many sightseeing tours in tourist boats, past the more famous riverside attractions such as the <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Houses of Parliament">Houses of Parliament</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a> as well as regular riverboat services co-ordinated by <a href="/wiki/London_River_Services" title="London River Services">London River Services</a>. London city Airport is situated on the Thames, in East London. Previously it was a dock.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_upper_river">The upper river</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The upper river">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In summer, passenger services operate along the entire non-tidal river from Oxford to Teddington. The two largest operators are <a href="/wiki/Salters_Steamers" title="Salters Steamers">Salters Steamers</a> and French Brothers. Salters operate services between <a href="/wiki/Folly_Bridge" title="Folly Bridge">Folly Bridge</a>, Oxford and Staines. The whole journey takes 4 days and requires several changes of boat.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> French Brothers operate passenger services between Maidenhead and Hampton Court.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\nAlong the course of the river a number of smaller private companies also offer river trips at Oxford, Wallingford, Reading and Hampton Court.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Many companies also provide boat hire on the river.\n</p><p>The leisure navigation and sporting activities on the river have given rise to a number of businesses including boatbuilding, marinas, ships chandlers and salvage services.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg/220px-City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg/440px-City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8442" data-file-height="4668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_London_skyline_from_London_City_Hall_-_Sept_2015_-_Crop_Aligned.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ferries operating on the Thames</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aerial_lift">Aerial lift</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Aerial lift">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_Air_Line_towers_24_May_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Emirates_Air_Line_towers_24_May_2012.jpg/220px-Emirates_Air_Line_towers_24_May_2012.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Emirates_Air_Line_towers_24_May_2012.jpg/330px-Emirates_Air_Line_towers_24_May_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Emirates_Air_Line_towers_24_May_2012.jpg/440px-Emirates_Air_Line_towers_24_May_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_Air_Line_towers_24_May_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>London\'s <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Air_Line_(cable_car)" title="Emirates Air Line (cable car)">Air Line</a> over the River Thames</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Air_Line_(cable_car)" title="Emirates Air Line (cable car)">Air Line</a> <a href="/wiki/Aerial_lift" title="Aerial lift">aerial cable system</a> over the Thames from the <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Peninsula" title="Greenwich Peninsula">Greenwich Peninsula</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Docks" title="Royal Docks">Royal Docks</a> has been in operation since the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_and_lifeboats">Police and lifeboats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Police and lifeboats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The river is policed by five police forces. The <a href="/wiki/Marine_Support_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Support Unit">Thames Division</a> is the River Police arm of London\'s <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Police">Metropolitan Police</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Surrey_Police" title="Surrey Police">Surrey Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thames_Valley_Police" title="Thames Valley Police">Thames Valley Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essex_Police" title="Essex Police">Essex Police</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kent_Police" title="Kent Police">Kent Police</a> have responsibilities on their parts of the river outside the metropolitan area. There is also a <a href="/wiki/London_Fire_Brigade" title="London Fire Brigade">London Fire Brigade</a> fire boat on the river. The river claims a number of lives each year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Marchioness_disaster" title="Marchioness disaster">Marchioness disaster</a> in 1989 when 51 people died, the <a href="/wiki/UK_government" class="mw-redirect" title="UK government">Government</a> asked the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_and_Coastguard_Agency" title="Maritime and Coastguard Agency">Maritime and Coastguard Agency</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_London_Authority" title="Port of London Authority">Port of London Authority</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_Lifeboat_Institution" title="Royal National Lifeboat Institution">Royal National Lifeboat Institution</a> (RNLI) to work together to set up a dedicated Search and Rescue service for the tidal River Thames. As a result, there are four <a href="/wiki/Lifeboat_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Lifeboat station">lifeboat stations</a> on the River Thames at <a href="/wiki/Teddington" title="Teddington">Teddington</a> (<a href="/wiki/Teddington_lifeboat_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Teddington lifeboat station">Teddington lifeboat station</a>), <a href="/wiki/Chiswick" title="Chiswick">Chiswick</a> (Chiswick lifeboat station), <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Embankment" title="Victoria Embankment">Victoria Embankment</a>/<a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Bridge" title="Waterloo Bridge">Waterloo Bridge</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tower_Lifeboat_Station" title="Tower Lifeboat Station">Tower Lifeboat Station</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Gravesend,_Kent" class="mw-redirect" title="Gravesend, Kent">Gravesend</a> (Gravesend lifeboat station).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Navigation">Navigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=River_Thames&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Navigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:River.thames.viewfromtowerbridge.london.arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" data-file-height="1274" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:River.thames.viewfromtowerbridge.london.arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pool of London looking west, from the high-level walkway on <a href="/wiki/Tower_Bridge" title="Tower Bridge">Tower Bridge</a>. Click on the picture for a longer description</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a data-file-width="800" data-file-height="531" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carpathia_Unloading_at_Tilbury_docks_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2091919.jpg" class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MV_Geeststroom_on_Thames_-_geograph.org.uk_-_360501.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/MV_Geeststroom_on_Thames_-_geograph.org.uk_-_360501.jpg/220px-MV_Geeststroom_on_Thames_-_geograph.org.uk_-_360501.jpg" width="220" height="147" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/MV_Geeststroom_on_Thames_-_geograph.org.uk_-_360501.jpg/440px-MV_Geeststroom_on_Thames_-_geograph.org.uk_-_360501.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MV_Geeststroom_on_Thames_-_geograph.org.uk_-_360501.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A ship heading downstream past <a href="/wiki/Coryton_Refinery" title="Coryton Refinery">Coryton Refinery</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:River_Thames_Rubbish_Trap,_London_-_Dec_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/River_Thames_Rubbish_Trap%2C_London_-_Dec_2008.jpg/220px-River_Thames_Rubbish_Trap%2C_London_-_Dec_2008.jpg" width="220" height="128"
